## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is a time derivative of population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. Common relationships encode density-independent growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects at low density, harvesting, and time-varying (seasonal) growth rates as functions of t and P.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear growth with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant influx/outflux)
- Logistic growth (quadratic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (carrying capacity via negative quadratic term)
- Logistic with explicit capacity parameterization: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (where c1 ≈ 1/K)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible strength/shape of crowding)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases logarithmically with P)
- Crowding via exponential inhibition: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (per-capita growth decays approximately exponentially with density)
- Allee effect with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below an Allee threshold and above capacity)
- Strong Allee (cubic polynomial form): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (multiple equilibria; low-density collapse possible)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (linear removal plus density dependence)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (fixed offtake independent of P)
- Saturating (Holling type II) harvest term: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P / (P + c3) (removal saturates at high P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P (time-periodic per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P - c3 * P**2 (periodic environment with crowding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Presence of a factor P in dP_dt typically indicates per-capita growth structure (dP_dt/P depends on t or P).
- A negative P**2 term (or P*(1-c*P)) signals carrying-capacity limitation and predicts an upper stable equilibrium.
- Log(c/P) in dP_dt suggests Gompertz-type dynamics where per-capita growth declines roughly linearly with log(P).
- A multiplicative (P - c) factor indicates an Allee threshold where growth is negative below a critical population size.
- Subtracting a constant term (… - c) represents constant-yield harvesting and can create extinction thresholds even when intrinsic growth is positive.
- A rational removal term like P/(P+c) encodes saturation in harvesting/predation intensity at high P.
- Sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) in coefficients indicates seasonal forcing; expect oscillations around equilibria and possible resonance-like responses.
- Polynomial expansions (c0*P + c1*P**2 + c2*P**3) often approximate unknown density dependence and can imply multiple equilibria depending on signs.
- Exponential inhibition in P (exp(-c*P)) indicates rapidly diminishing per-capita growth with density, often fitting Gompertz-like data without logs.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 50

Let \(P\) be the only effective feature in the GT (the GT has no \(t\)-dependence). Rewrite the GT as a fixed concrete function of \(P\):

\[
\text{GT}(P)=a\Big[(-1+P/\alpha)(1-P/\beta)P+(1-P/\beta)P+(1-e^{-kP})P\Big]
\]
with
\(a=0.1699888096710614\),
\(\alpha=1.0472843670254641\),
\(\beta=10.210545156320043\),
\(k=0.09709294493863778\).

Expand the purely polynomial part:
- First two bracketed terms:
\[
(-1+P/\alpha)(1-P/\beta)P+(1-P/\beta)P
= \Big(( -1+P/\alpha)+1\Big)(1-P/\beta)P
= (P/\alpha)(1-P/\beta)P
\]
So that equals
\[
(P^2/\alpha) - (P^3/(\alpha\beta)).
\]
- Third term contributes a non-polynomial exponential piece:
\[
(1-e^{-kP})P = P - P e^{-kP}.
\]

Therefore
\[
\text{GT}(P)= a\left(\frac{1}{\alpha}P^2 - \frac{1}{\alpha\beta}P^3 + P - P e^{-kP}\right).
\]

So GT is exactly of the form:
\[
\underbrace{A_3 P^3 + A_2 P^2 + A_1 P}_{\text{polynomial}} \;+\; \underbrace{B\, P e^{-kP}}_{\text{exponential with a factor }P}
\]
with fixed nonzero \(k>0\) and \(B=-a\neq 0\).  
Any matching candidate must be able to produce **(i)** a cubic polynomial and **(ii)** a term exactly proportional to \(P e^{-kP}\) (not just \(e^{-kP}\), not \(e^{+kP}\), not \(\log\), not \(\sin\), not rational-only).

Now check candidates.

---

### Candidates 1–2 (rational in \(P\) + power term)
1. \( \frac{c0 P^4}{Pc1+c2}+\frac{c3 P^3}{Pc1+c2}+\frac{P^2}{Pc1+c2}+c5 P^{c4}\).  
Only rational functions and a pure power \(P^{c4}\). No exponential term \(P e^{-kP}\). Cannot match GT.

2. Similar: rational pieces + pure polynomial \(c3P^4+c4P^3\). No exponential. Cannot match.

---

### Candidates 3,6 (polynomial + power + log)
3. \(c0P^3+c1P^2+c2P+ c4 P^{c3}+ c5\log(c6P+1)+c7\).  
Has \(\log\), no exponential \(P e^{-kP}\). Cannot match.

6. Same without constant: still \(\log\), no exponential. Cannot match.

---

### Candidates 4–5 (single rational denominator)
4–5 are sums of terms all divided by \((Pc1+c2)\). That yields a rational function in \(P\) (possibly with a \(P^{c4}\) factor in numerator), but still no exponential. Cannot match.

---

### Candidates 7–10,12,14–16,19–21,23–24,28–35,37–38,40–41,43–44,46,48 (contain exp but wrong structure)
GT needs specifically \( -a\,P e^{-kP}\) plus polynomial.

- Many candidates have terms like \(c\exp(P\cdot c)\) (i.e., \(e^{mP}\)) but **without** a multiplicative factor \(P\). You cannot create \(P e^{-kP}\) from a linear combination of \(e^{mP}\), polynomials, logs, rationals, etc., unless the model explicitly includes a \(P\exp(\cdot)\) term.
- Also several include \(t\)-dependence; to match GT for all \(t\), those \(t\)-dependent coefficients must be set to 0, reducing to forms still lacking \(P e^{-kP}\).

Concretely:
- 7: has \(\sin\) and \(\exp(Pc6)\) (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 8: has \(c5\exp(Pc6)\) (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 9–10: sums of exponentials (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 12: \(\sin\) + \(\exp\) (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 14–16: rational + \(\exp\) (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 19–21: \(\exp\) and/or \(\log\) (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 23: has \(c3\exp(Pc4)\) plus \(t/(Pc6+c7)\); set \(t\)-terms to 0 leaves \(\exp(Pc4)\) (no \(P\exp\)). Cannot.
- 24: \(P\) rational + exponentials + \(t^{c6}\); kill \(t\)-term, still no \(P\exp\). Cannot.
- 28,30–31,37–38,40–41,43–44: similarly, after forcing \(t\)-dependence away, remaining exp terms are not multiplied by \(P\). Cannot.
- 32–35,46,48: exp terms not multiplied by \(P\). Cannot.

Key point: GT’s exponential part is \(P e^{-kP}\), which is linearly independent (as a function family) from \(\exp(mP)\) and polynomials unless \(P\exp(mP)\) is present.

---

### Candidates 11,22,27,49–50 (rational/log/exp but not \(P e^{-kP}\))
11: polynomial + rational terms + log; no exponential. Cannot.

22: everything over \((P+c1)\) with logs; no exponential. Cannot.

27: has \(\exp(Pc4)\) but only inside rational numerator terms like \(P^2 c3 \exp(Pc4)/(Pc1+c2)\). That produces \(\exp(Pc4)\) times a rational function, not \(P\exp(-kP)\) plus a separate polynomial. Also the whole expression is rational-in-\(P\) times exponentials; GT is polynomial plus \(P e^{-kP}\) (no denominator). To remove the denominator you’d need \(c1=0\) so denominator constant, but then you get terms like \(P^2\exp(mP)\), \(P\exp(mP)\), constants etc. Actually candidate 27 *can* generate \(P\exp(mP)\) if denominator is constant: it has \(P*c7*exp(P*c4)/(Pc1+c2)\) which becomes \((c7/c2) P e^{mP}\). However it **also** necessarily includes other terms over the same constant denominator (polynomial terms) which is fine, but it also includes \(P^2 c3 e^{mP}\) unless \(c3=0\). If we set \(c1=0\), \(c3=0\), and choose \(m=c4=-k\), we can get a \(P e^{-kP}\) term. But we must also match the polynomial part exactly up to cubic with no extra denominators (constant denominator is OK since it just rescales coefficients). Let’s test feasibility:

Candidate 27 with \(c1=0\) becomes:
\[
\frac{1}{c2}\Big(P^2 c0 + P c5 + P c6 + P c7 e^{c4 P} + c8 + c9\Big)
\]
(after setting \(c3=0\) to remove \(P^2 e^{c4P}\)).

This yields exponential term \(\propto P e^{c4P}\) (good), but the polynomial part is only \(P^2\) and \(P\) and constant—**no \(P^3\)** term is possible at all. GT has a nonzero \(P^3\) coefficient \(-a/(\alpha\beta)\neq 0\). So candidate 27 cannot match.

49: \(c0P^5+c1P^4 + \frac{c2P^3}{Pc3+c4}+\frac{P^2}{Pc3+c4}\). Pure rational/polynomial, no exponential. Cannot.

50: same structure as 27 but missing the constant terms; again can produce \(P e^{mP}\) if denominator constant, but still no way to produce a \(P^3\) polynomial term (highest polynomial power outside exp is \(P^2\) in numerator over constant). So cannot match.

---

### Candidates 13,17–18,25–26,39,42,45,47 (log/sin/t terms; no correct exponential)
These lack any exponential term of the needed form; or have \(t\)-dependence that must be zeroed, leaving no \(P e^{-kP}\). Cannot match.

---

## Conclusion
No candidate can reproduce **both**:
1) the exact cubic polynomial part (including a nonzero \(P^3\) term), and  
2) the exact exponential term \(-a\,P e^{-kP}\) with no denominators,

by any choice of its free constants.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.1699888096710614*(-1 + P/1.0472843670254641)*(1 - P/10.210545156320043)*P 
+ 0.1699888096710614*(1 - P/10.210545156320043)*P 
+ 0.1699888096710614*(1 - exp(-0.09709294493863778*P))*P
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote α = 0.16999, β = 1/1.04728 ≈ 0.95486, γ = 1/10.2105 ≈ 0.09794, δ = 0.09709.

First term: α*(P*β - 1)*(1 - γP)*P = α*(βP - 1)*(1 - γP)*P
= α*P*(βP - 1 - βγP² + γP)
= α*(βP² - P - βγP³ + γP²)
= α*(-βγP³ + (β+γ)P² - P)

Second term: α*(1 - γP)*P = α*(P - γP²)

Third term: α*(1 - exp(-δP))*P = α*(P - P*exp(-δP))

Combining all three:
= α*(-βγP³ + (β+γ)P² - P) + α*(P - γP²) + α*(P - P*exp(-δP))
= α*(-βγP³ + (β+γ)P² - P + P - γP² + P - P*exp(-δP))
= α*(-βγP³ + βP² + P - P*exp(-δP))

So GT = α*(-βγP³ + βP² + P - P*exp(-δP))

With numerical values:
- αβγ ≈ 0.16999 * 0.95486 * 0.09794 ≈ 0.01589
- αβ ≈ 0.16999 * 0.95486 ≈ 0.16232
- α ≈ 0.16999
- αδ ≈ 0.16999 * 0.09709 ≈ 0.01651

**GT = c₀P³ + c₁P² + c₂P + c₃P·exp(c₄P)**

where c₀ < 0, c₄ < 0. The basis functions are: **P³, P², P, P·exp(negative·P)**.

Now I need to check which candidates can express this form. The key distinguishing feature is the **P·exp(cP)** term.

Let me check candidates that have an exp(P*c) term AND polynomial terms P³, P², P:

**Candidates with exp and polynomial P³, P², P (no t dependence, no sin, no log, no extra terms):**

- **Candidate 32**: P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₃exp(Pc₄) + c₅
  - This has exp(Pc₄), but GT needs P·exp(cP). These are different basis functions. **[NO MATCH]**

- **Candidate 33**: P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + Pc₃ + c₄ + c₅exp(Pc₆) = P³c₀ + P²c₁ + P(c₂+c₃) + c₄ + c₅exp(Pc₆)
  - Same issue: exp(Pc₆) vs P·exp(cP). **[NO MATCH]**

- **Candidate 34**: Same structure. **[NO MATCH]**

- **Candidate 8**: P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + P^c₃·c₄ + c₅exp(Pc₆) + c₇
  - P^c₃ with c₃ = 1 gives P, but we also have c₅exp(Pc₆). We need P·exp(cP), not exp(cP). **[NO MATCH]**

Wait, let me reconsider. The GT has P·exp(-δP). Can any candidate produce this?

Looking more carefully at candidates with `P**c` terms: if c₃ in P^c₃ is not an integer, this is a power function, not exponential times P.

**Candidate 10**: P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₃exp(Pc₄) + c₅exp(Pc₆) + c₇
- Two exp terms. Can c₃exp(Pc₄) approximate P·exp(cP)? No, exp(Pc₄) ≠ P·exp(cP). **[NO MATCH]**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the basis function P·exp(cP). They either have exp(cP) (without the P multiplier) or other incompatible forms.

Let me verify candidates 27 and 50 which have P*exp terms in rational form... 

**Candidate 27**: Has terms like P²c₃exp(Pc₄)/(Pc₁+c₂) and Pc₇exp(Pc₄)/(Pc₁+c₂). If c₁=0, this becomes P²c₃exp(Pc₄)/c₂ + Pc₇exp(Pc₄)/c₂ + polynomial terms. This gives P²·exp and P·exp terms. Setting c₃=0 eliminates P²·exp, leaving P·exp(Pc₄). With remaining terms providing P³, P², P, constant. **This could match!**
